{"nick":"joepie91","message":"the Promise itself is synchronously returned - the value or error it'll contain usually only exists later, and you can act upon that change by attaching a .then/.catch/etc handler","date":"2016-03-14T03:28:30.516Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"they can be composed (eg. with Promise.all, which basically means \"make a combined promise that resolves/rejects when all the promises in this array have done so\")","date":"2016-03-14T03:28:51.215Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"they automatically propagate errors upwards until you handle them, much like synchronously thrown errors","date":"2016-03-14T03:29:05.347Z","type":"message"}
